I had an emergency where my dog had cut herself deeply, and thankfully we were seen immediately that day. It had been about 10 minutes before closing on a Sunday. I'm so grateful that they were open and able to see my pup!

The only downside is that the front staff are constantly swamped with phone calls and clients that I felt I was being rushed out the door when I had came back to get her stitches out and had some non-urgent questions I wanted to ask. Being a first time dog owner it's really important for me to feel like I can get that information from my vets office.

I used to go to Alderbrook in Santa Rosa, which was convenient and much smaller than this office but had 3 and sometimes 4 people working the front with only one vet. In addition to Dr. Piper‚Äôs great car, I feel that my dogs have received exceptional care from all the veterinarians working there. Recently I have had the opportunity to have my dog assessed by their Rehabilitation Specialist, Kristen Hagler, RVT, CCRP. < review>
This place is the best auto auction I‚Äôve seen. The reason is simple - all the vehicles are donated. Who donates their old cars?  Wealthier people tend to be the ones who donate their cars, and wealthier people tend to take better care of their cars because they can afford to maintain them and get them fixed properly right when they have trouble. Poorer people tend to wait on maintenance because they can barely afford to, oftentimes they try to fix their own vehicles or trust friends or otherwise do things that wear cars out faster.
There is a distinct difference in a car that was donated as opposed to wrecked, stolen, or who knows how a non-donated car finds itself at an auto-auction, but I can tell you that there is a difference and you can feel it. There is a sense of bad juju you can feel in a car that was towed, wrecked, or recovered stolen. At Capital City Auto Auction, all the cars were donated. Think about that for a minute. It makes a difference. I‚Äôve bought 7 cars and an RV so far and every single one of my purchases turned out well so far.</review>

<Resp>None<//Resp>< review>
So i have very mixed feelings for this place. Overall, i would say it's good. There are a few things that just stand out and have a negative impact on ones overall satisfaction.
Capital City Auto Auction's vehicle inventory is so diverse. You'll see Just about every kind of car comes through here. From cars that you see every day,  nicer cars,  several reliable models,  some that by all means shouldn't have made it this far in time, to models that will make your head explode as you are yelling  "who the heck donates a car like that!.?"
With that being said,  several times I find myself horrified at some of the things I see. This is all just in photos, but it's pretty close to a pig farm. A car whos previous owner cared for very well... looks close to new inside (or out) until it's handled here. Mud all over the driver side carpeting and and pedals. Fresh coffee spills on dash and upholstery.  There have been photos of vehicles sitting in the middle of a rain/mud puddle just waiting for the operator to jump back in with his muddy shoes. There is clearly no regard to mind this frequent occurrence nor the respect for the cars or so to be owners. Be prepared to clean your purchases.

The COVID copout here is that they wont let you see the cars in person. Its all outdoors, I just dont see the difference in previewing the car, as it relates to contact,  as when the vehicle is picked up. So watch the pictures very closely, as they are no help whatsoever with wetting cars. Remember, they are not being washed! Aside from the enormous waste of water,  they are just trying to make it look better so what you see is not necessarily what you get. Three purchases only to find after purchase that they were highly oxidised. Of course they still wet the car if the windows are inoperable and down. Cats probably live in those cars, but all the dust and mud from the forklifts and tow trucks buzzing by will mask that though. Buy some gravel!
The fees are another concern. Like a smog cert fee. Sounds valid, it‚Äôs smogged, right?  The auction DOES NOT PAY FOR OR SMOG the vehicle, so this is a corrupt and easy way to nickel and dime for nothing. It‚Äôs dishonest and condemnable.

When you try to get more info on a car, you'll be pacified with a generic response along the lines of "we don't diagnose vehicles" which I would believe if they weren't throwing them on a lift.
Oh my first taste of recklessness came on a forklift. My heart just about stopped. The car I had purchased was low or out of gas, so instead of bringing a gas can over,  it was lifted with a forklift from the front (very much the wrong way), causing damage to the front end control arms and the fresh metal underneath was from its weight sitting improperly on the forks, but i made no effort to bring this up in any way knowing what a response would consist of.

The following are also junk/gouge fees- the Internet fee, though it's the one and only option for now, and the kick ya in the teeth credit card fee! They will not take more than $500 in cash, but will allow the rest of it on a credit card/debit card for a nominal fee at 3%.
If you've read this far,  know that they are as is, but there is a chance that after you buy a car, something happens to it and in my personal experience had an additional problem that was marked on the windshield before i picked it up (i could smell the fresh ink) but after an encounter With forky the lift/driver. A new problem not listed listed anywhere prior and it was not on there when they took  photos but somehow diagnosed it auction day, the best was having the serpentine belt shredded. Yup, they got yard games.
I would, however, go for another car here if the right one comes along, but i can candidly say that I AM SCARED TO. Same risk in an end of life car in most cars, but good ones are totally available. It can definitely be a good experience with favorable outcomes.
3 stars solid.<//review>

So your total price could easily be double your bid price.  But  you should know this going in and bid accordingly.  Its just the owners financial strategy to realize maximum return on the sales with minimum return to the charities that are supposed to benefit from the donated cars.

Ive never bought a car there that i could drive home without having to stop for overheating, bad fuel pump or any myriad of other problems.  Several times i had to tow a runs and drives car out of there.

So i had to come back the next day with a battery.  That worked for about two blocks.  It needed an alternator.  The check engine light was on none of which was disclosed.   And it had 3 absolutely flat tires  which wasnt disclosed or shown in the photos. I went to this location on Tuesday with my boyfriend to try out the food since it seemed like a really good place to eat Mexican food at. We were completely wrong. We ordered online, there was a 35 minute wait for our food, which we did not mind. When the 35 minutes came by, I went into the store. She just kept looking at me and then stared at my phone. I asked her if she needed the email for confirmation and with attitude she said yes. She then wrote down my name and told me to wait outside. I waiting for 10 minutes after the 35 minutes I was required to wait. I went inside and since she was not around, I waited for her to come back. Before talking to her, the client she was talking to said he had been waiting for an hour already. I asked her "how much longer until I receive my order" and she just stared at me and nodded and walked away. Meanwhile she went to help another client to look for his order, he mentioned that he was waiting for an hour and 30 minutes which seems ridiculous for the fact that it was a pick up order and people in the drive thru and walking into the store were getting their orders faster. This was one of my worse customer experiences at your location and they should properly  train their employees because our money is paying their bills.< /text>

<GmapID>0x80c2c5118c200607:0x13bdafa822b1f768<//GmapID><user>103554035274985144447<//user>< text>
I've tried the aguachiles tostada, fish tacos, carne asada tacos, chicken tacos, potatoe tacos, shrimp cocktail, asada sope, chicken sope, horchata, and cucumber water. I love the fish tacos the best. Their meat isn't lean, so if you don't like eating fat, you'll have to pick it out of your food like I do. If you like spicy foods try the aguachiles and get that cucumber water with mint and chia seeds. It's the most refreshing drink! A good meatless option are the potatoe tacos, they're delicious.
If you go on a Tuesday, the line goes all the way outside and it was way too crowded to eat inside because the fish tacos are 99cents each. On Thursdays the meat tacos are 99cents each.

*UPDATE* Feb 2018
I recently also tried the barbacoa tacos, pi√±a agua fresca and strawberry agua fresca. All three were really good.  I gave it another go with the carne asada and chicken and ordered sopes but their meat still isn't clean so I couldn't eat 80% of it. I even ASK before ordering if their meat has "cuero". The cashier thought I meant skin and had me ask one of the cooks and he said it was clean (but it wasn't like always) -.- so I'll stick to the fish tacos and barbacoa!

*UPDATE* March 2018
Extremely lean meat in my sope!!! I ordered a carne asada sope and I FINALLY got no fat with my meat, it was delicious! I hope they keep it up!!!<//text>

<UserId.>115246144325654585948< /UserId.>< name>
Christopher Lui<//name>
<time>1499653685625</time><rating>4< /rating>< Review>
Very tasty, reasonably cheap fish tacos.Nicely fried, flavorful, with tasty sides and sauce.  It seems like they have dollar fish tacos on Tuesday which I will for sure be coming back for.
I found that other items on the menu were closer to average. The pastor and carne asada tacos I had were both relatively tasty, but the meat itself didn't seem to be of great quality. The "crab" ceviche is actually made of imitation crab(I should have known from the cheap price). The strawberry agua fresca is delicious and not too sweet. Their condiment and sides bar is extensive, with radishes, onions, and large banana peppers available.

The service is just okay, and we had to wait a decent amount of time for our food.

Overall I would definitely come back and probably just order the fish tacos.<//Review>
